data-reactid=".2dk3abu0zy8.3.2.$main-minute.0.0.0.2.0" itemprop="title"><span data-reactid=".2dk3abu0zy8.3.2.$main-minute.0.0.0.2.0.0">The Sanders and Clinton campaigns are in the middle of a Twitter flame war and it\xe2\x80\x99s great.</span></h1><div class="minute-content" data-reactid=".2dk3abu0zy8.3.2.$main-minute.0.0.0.2.1"><p>Both Hillary and Bernie have done their level best to grin at one another over clenched teeth and avoid the kind of mudslinging that has characterized the Republican primary.</p><aside class="signal pull-right hide" id="signal-129105"></aside><p>But with one contentious contest in the rearview mirror and another fast approaching, their two campaigns are starting to get a bit feisty. Hours before the two meet in a televised town hall in New Hampshire, Sanders\xe2\x80\x99s Twitter account sent this:\xc2\xa0</p><figure class="article-embed"><blockquote class="twitter-tweet" data-lang="en"><p dir="ltr" lang="en">Most progressives that I know don\'t raise millions of dollars from Wall Street.</p>\xe2\x80\x94 Bernie Sanders (@BernieSanders) <a href="https://twitter.com/BernieSanders/status/694967503995457536" rel="nofollow" target="_blank">February 3, 2016</a></blockquote> <script async="" charset="utf-8" src="//platform.twitter.com/widgets.js"></script></figure><p>It was the first in a <a href="https://twitter.com/BernieSanders/status/694970390456696832" rel="nofollow" target="_blank">series of subtweets</a> directed squarely at Clinton questioning her progressive bona fides.<br/></p><p>Well, Clinton\xe2\x80\x99s team was not about to let Bernie have the last word, and they clapped back hard:</p><figure class="article-embed"><blockquote class="twitter-tweet" data-lang="en"><p dir="ltr" lang="en">2) Now, if you do want to make it about who\'s a "real progressive," <a href="https://twitter.com/BernieSanders" rel="nofollow" target="_blank">@BernieSanders</a>, what were you on these days? <a href="https://t.co/8Q6hANYPhh" rel="nofollow" target="_blank">pic.twitter.com/8Q6hANYPhh</a></p>\xe2\x80\x94 Hillary Clinton (@HillaryClinton) <a href="https://twitter.com/HillaryClinton/status/695000617308274689" rel="nofollow" target="_blank">February 3, 2016</a></blockquote> <script async="" charset="utf-8" src="//platform.twitter.com/widgets.js"></script></figure><figure class="article-embed"><blockquote class="twitter-tweet" data-lang="en"><p dir="ltr" lang="en">4) Hillary\'s not running to make a point\xe2\x80\x94she\'s running to make a difference. She\'ll keep doing that. Please feel free to keep tweeting.</p>\xe2\x80\x94 Hillary Clinton (@HillaryClinton) <a href="https://twitter.com/HillaryClinton/status/695001261087842305" rel="nofollow" target="_blank">February 3, 2016</a></blockquote> <script async="" charset="utf-8" src="//platform.twitter.com/widgets.js"></script></figure><p>The Democratic debates have so far been cordial and substantive, which makes for smart politics but lousy television. If you miss the fireworks though, give both these candidates a follow.\xc2\xa0</p></div></div><div class="sharebox sharebox-minute" data-reactid=".2dk3abu0zy8.3.2.$main-minute.0.0.0.3"><div data-reactid=".2dk3abu0zy8.3.3.0.$0.1.0.0.2.0" itemprop="title"><span data-reactid=".2dk3abu0zy8.3.3.0.$0.1.0.0.2.0.0">How rude of Bernie Sanders to bring up the Vietnam War.</span></h1><div class="minute-content" data-reactid=".2dk3abu0zy8.3.3.0.$0.1.0.0.2.1"><p>Hillary Clinton made Henry Kissinger an issue in the Democratic primary by citing his praise of her tenure as secretary of state. In last night\xe2\x80\x99s debate, Sanders took the opportunity to remind viewers that Kissinger is not seen as a sage by everyone. As noted by Gawker, when Sanders brought up Vietnam, <a href="http://gawker.com/moderator-accidentally-whispers-oh-god-into-mic-when-1758651605" rel="nofollow" target="_blank">one of the PBS moderators whispered</a>, \xe2\x80\x9cOh, god\xe2\x80\x9d into her mic.</p><aside class="signal pull-right hide" id="signal-129813"></aside><p>Now, the moderator (it sounded like Judy Woodruff) could have been responding to any number of things. But it\xe2\x80\x99s easy to make the argument that this hot mic moment reveals a deep\xc2\xa0status quo bias at PBS. Over the decades, Kissinger has been a <a href="http://www.pbs.org/newshour/bb/middle_east-july-dec06-mideast_07-18/" rel="nofollow" target="_blank">frequent guest</a> on the flagship <i>Newshour</i> program, where he is invariably treated as a wise man. In the world of PBS newscasting, it\xe2\x80\x99s simply in bad taste to bring up the possibility that Kissinger\xe2\x80\x94based on his policies towards Vietnam, Cambodia, Chile, Bangladesh, and other countries\xe2\x80\x94might deserve <a href="http://www.amazon.com/Trial-Henry-Kissinger-Christopher-Hitchens/dp/145552297X" rel="nofollow" target="_blank">the title of war criminal</a>. Going against the grain of this status quo bias, which exists at other media organizations as well, is going to be a major challenge for Bernie Sanders.\xc2\xa0</p></div></div><div class="sharebox sharebox-minute" data-reactid=".2dk3abu0zy8.3.3.0.$0.1.0.0.3"><div class="sharebox-inner" data-reactid=".2dk3abu0zy8.3.3.0.$0.1.0.0.3.0"><a class="sharebox-cell" data-reactid=".2dk3abu0zy8.3.3.0.$1.1.0.0.2.0" itemprop="title"><span data-reactid=".2dk3abu0zy8.3.3.0.$1.1.0.0.2.0.0">Hillaryland, for once, is playing it smart.</span></h1><div class="minute-content" data-reactid=".2dk3abu0zy8.3.3.0.$1.1.0.0.2.1"><p>If Bernie Sanders is the most on-message candidate in the 2016 race, if he has a penchant for returning time and again to his overarching worldview, and if he has abided by the plain principles of respect and positivity that he set out early in his candidacy, then Clinton has already tried several different approaches and messages in this young campaign, with the result that you never quite know which Clinton you\xe2\x80\x99re going to get. There was some speculation that she would hit Sanders hard at Thursday night\xe2\x80\x99s debate, to blunt his momentum following an overwhelming victory in New Hampshire. And earlier in the day we got a glimpse of the kinds of cutting attacks her campaign can deploy, with supporter John Lewis coldly <a href="/minutes/129711/clinton-supporters-going-bernie-sanderss-role-civil-rights-movement">excising</a> Sanders from any involvement in the civil rights movement.</p><aside class="signal pull-right hide" id="signal-129793"></aside><p>But as in 2008, when her attacks on the broadly liked Barack Obama fell flat, going negative on Sanders has only served to alienate liberals that Clinton ultimately needs to convince. It seems Clinton finally understands this; in the debate last night she insistently highlighted her areas of agreement with Sanders, lauded the ambitions of the progressive movement, and stuck close to Obama, the most unifying figure in the party. It may make for a dull debate, but it\xe2\x80\x99s a long-term game plan that makes sense for a candidate whose main problem is a progressive base that doesn\xe2\x80\x99t trust her.</p></div></div><div class="sharebox sharebox-minute" data-reactid=".2dk3abu0zy8.3.3.0.$1.1.0.0.3"><div class="sharebox-inner" data-reactid=".2dk3abu0zy8.3.3.0.$1.1.0.0.3.0"><a In both instances, the Cruz campaign stood by their guys.\xc2\xa0</p><aside class="signal pull-right hide" id="signal-129807"></aside><p>Team Cruz is not being cool at all about Amy Lindsay, though. data-reactid=".2dk3abu0zy8.3.3.0.$4.1.0.0.2"><h1 class="minute-title" data-reactid=".2dk3abu0zy8.3.3.0.$4.1.0.0.2.0" itemprop="title"><span data-reactid=".2dk3abu0zy8.3.3.0.$4.1.0.0.2.0.0">Bernie killed it on the final debate question and Hillary... didn\xe2\x80\x99t.</span></h1><div class="minute-content" data-reactid=".2dk3abu0zy8.3.3.0.$4.1.0.0.2.1"><p>PBS elevated this question from a random Facebook person: \xe2\x80\x9cCan you name two leaders, one American and one foreign, who would influence your policy decisions?\xe2\x80\x9d Sanders could have trolled all of conservative media by answering \xe2\x80\x9cNeville Chamberlain.\xe2\x80\x9d He didn\xe2\x80\x99t do that, but he also did more than name uncontroversial dead presidents. His answer was inspiring, a case against defeatism.</p><aside class="signal pull-right hide" id="signal-129786"></aside><p>Franklin Delano Roosevelt\xe2\x80\x99s famous line\xe2\x80\x94\xe2\x80\x9cThe only thing we have to fear is fear itself\xe2\x80\x9d\xe2\x80\x94was \xe2\x80\x9ca profound statement that gave the American people the courage to believe that, yes, we could get out of that terrible Depression. And then what he did is redefine the role of government.\xe2\x80\x9d Herbert Hoover had argued helping needy people was not the role of the government. \xe2\x80\x9cAnd what FDR said was, \xe2\x80\x98Yeah, it is.\xe2\x80\x99\xe2\x80\x9d Sanders then shifted to a pitch for his candidacy, and a defense against Clinton\xe2\x80\x99s criticism that his policies are not achievable: \xe2\x80\x9cThat\xe2\x80\x99s what I see our campaign is about, right now, in this particular moment of serious crisis, saying to the American people, \xe2\x80\x98Dont give up on the political process. \xc2\xa0... If we engage and get involved, <i>yeah</i>, we can have health care for all people,\xe2\x80\x9d and free college tuition, etc. Then he cited Winston Churchill, though \xe2\x80\x9c[his]\xc2\xa0<span>politics were not my politics,\xe2\x80\x9d for rallying the British people.</span></p><p>His answer ended on a pleasant, patriotic note, just as the debate was almost over. Hillary began her response by clearing her throat, which was not a good sign. She said FDR was great, but she also liked Nelson Mandela \xe2\x80\x9cfor his generosity of heart, for his understanding of the need for reconciliation.\xe2\x80\x9d That\xe2\x80\x99s it. Then she started attacking Sanders for criticizing President Obama\xe2\x80\x99s leadership.\xc2\xa0<span>Clinton did get applause when she said Obama \xe2\x80\x9cdoesn\xe2\x80\x99t get the credit he deserves.\xe2\x80\x9d But it was still tone-deaf, taking a moment that was about America being awesome and turning it into a fight over cable news hits. And it underscored the memes of the campaign\xe2\x80\x94that Sanders has inspiring ideas, and that Clinton knows how to score points.</span></p></div></div><div class="sharebox sharebox-minute" itemprop="title"><span data-reactid=".2dk3abu0zy8.3.3.0.$5.1.0.0.2.0.0">Clinton and Sanders spar over deporting immigrant children. </span></h1><div class="minute-content" data-reactid=".2dk3abu0zy8.3.3.0.$5.1.0.0.2.1"><p>Both the Democratic candidates have come out in support of comprehensive immigration reform, including a path to citizenship. But Thursday\xe2\x80\x99s debate exposed a clear difference in immigration policy.</p><aside class="signal pull-right hide" id="signal-129769"></aside><p>In a combative exchange, Bernie Sanders reiterated his refusal to deport children to the \xe2\x80\x9chorrendously violent areas of Honduras and neighboring countries\xe2\x80\x9d they are now fleeing in record numbers. Clinton, on the other hand, said that while she was against the Obama administration\xe2\x80\x99s \xe2\x80\x9cinhumane\xe2\x80\x9d\xc2\xa0<a href="http://thinkprogress.org/immigration/2016/01/12/3738358/dems-pushback-obama-raids/" rel="nofollow" target="_blank">deportation raids</a>, she would not come out against child deportation in general, preferring instead to back <a href="http://www.huffingtonpost.com/entry/immigration-legal-counsel_us_56bca5e3e4b0c3c550503082" rel="nofollow" target="_blank">a proposal currently being put forward in Congress</a> to provide undocumented minors guaranteed legal services, a right they do not currently enjoy.\xc2\xa0<span>\xe2\x80\x9cWe should be deporting criminals, not hard-working immigrant families,\xe2\x80\x9d she said.\xc2\xa0</span></p><figure class="article-embed"><div class="video-wrapper" style="padding-bottom: 56.25%;"><iframe allowfullscreen="" frameborder="0" height="315" src="//www.youtube.com/embed/hOB5RWQ-rg4" width="560"></iframe></div></figure><p><span>What\xe2\x80\x99s striking about her response is not simply the willingness to ship children back to a region mired in </span><a href="http://borderfactcheck.com/" rel="nofollow" target="_blank">conflict-level bloodshed</a><span>. It\xe2\x80\x99s her insistence on sticking to the very tough-on crime pose that helped foster the present situation in the first place. Especially in El Salvador, today\xe2\x80\x99s gang violence </span><a href="http://www.npr.org/sections/goatsandsoda/2015/10/05/445382231/how-el-salvador-fell-into-a-web-of-gang-violence" rel="nofollow" target="_blank">directly stems</a><span>\xc2\xa0from the Clinton-era policy of aggressively deporting felons.</span><br/></p></div></div><div class="sharebox sharebox-minute" class="minute-content" data-reactid=".2dk3abu0zy8.3.3.0.$7.1.0.0.2.1"><p>In the foreign policy section of tonight\xe2\x80\x99s Democratic debate, Sanders has\xc2\xa0sounded a bit like my AP U.S. History teacher, who was cool as hell and introduced me to Howard Zinn and the Grateful Dead.\xc2\xa0He\xe2\x80\x99s talked about\xc2\xa0Mosaddegh, the democratically elected Iranian leader that the United States overthrew in 1953. And he\xe2\x80\x99s talked <i>a lot </i>about Henry Kissinger.\xc2\xa0</p><aside class="signal pull-right hide" id="signal-129783"></aside><p>Sanders may have exaggerated some of the negative consequences of some of Kissinger\xe2\x80\x99s actions and policies\xe2\x80\x94the idea that the opening to China was bad because it cost American jobs seems like an overstatement. B<span>ut he\xe2\x80\x99s totally right to call Clinton\xe2\x80\x99s relationship with Kissinger into question, as his foreign policy was disastrous and led to incredibly destructive consequences around the world, from Chile to Cambodia. (For more on the relationship between Clinton and Kissinger, this </span><a href="http://www.thenation.com/article/henry-kissinger-hillary-clintons-tutor-in-war-and-peace/" rel="nofollow" target="_blank">story</a><span> is a good place to start.)\xc2\xa0</span></p><p>Sanders has struggled to articulate a core foreign policy throughout the campaign. Though he\xe2\x80\x99s made small strides, it\xe2\x80\x99s clear that he still isn\xe2\x80\x99t particularly comfortable venturing out on his own. So he\xe2\x80\x99s sticking to his core message, which is that Hillary Clinton\xe2\x80\x99s foreign policy judgment has led to disastrous, unforeseen consequences. And her relationship with Kissinger is a proxy for that argument.</p><figure class="article-embed"><div class="video-wrapper" style="padding-bottom: 56.25%;"><iframe allowfullscreen="" frameborder="0" data-reactid=".2dk3abu0zy8.3.3.0.$8.1.0.0.2.1"><p>David Axelrod, who ran Obama\xe2\x80\x99s winning presidential campaign in 2008, made a shrewd observation on Twitter:</p><figure class="article-embed"><blockquote class="twitter-tweet" data-lang="en"><p dir="ltr" lang="en">Even when <a href="https://twitter.com/SenSanders" rel="nofollow" target="_blank">@SenSanders</a> was clearly looking to start a fight, <a href="https://twitter.com/HillaryClinton" rel="nofollow" target="_blank">@hillaryclinton</a> chose to hug not slug. All stiletto tonight. <a href="https://twitter.com/hashtag/DemDebate?src=hash" rel="nofollow" target="_blank">#DemDebate</a></p>\xe2\x80\x94 David Axelrod (@davidaxelrod) <a href="https://twitter.com/davidaxelrod/status/697981821099864065" rel="nofollow" target="_blank">February 12, 2016</a></blockquote>\n<script async="" charset="utf-8" src="//platform.twitter.com/widgets.js"></script></figure><aside class="signal pull-right hide" id="signal-129780"></aside><p><span>It\xe2\x80\x99s exactly right that as the underdog and challenger, Sanders is trying to differentiate himself from Clinton, to give people a reason to vote for him. Clinton, by contrast, is trying to suggest that she and Sanders agree on goals, but she\xe2\x80\x99s more adept at achieving those goals. Clinton also doesn\xe2\x80\x99t need to attack Sanders directly because she has many more surrogates in the party who will do that for her.\xc2\xa0</span></p><p>\xe2\x80\x9cWe\xe2\x80\x99re in vigorous agreement here,\xe2\x80\x9d Clinton said at one point. When Sanders suggested he and Clinton differed on expanding Social Security, Clinton responded, \xe2\x80\x9cI think it\xe2\x80\x99s fair to say we don\xe2\x80\x99t have a disagreement.\xe2\x80\x9d After outlining her policy of focusing on low-income seniors, she ended by saying, \xe2\x80\x9cWe have no disagreement about the need to buttress Social Security, get more revenue into the program. ...I think we\xe2\x80\x99re in vigorous agreement here. ...<span>We\xe2\x80\x99re going to end up in the same place.\xe2\x80\x9d\xc2\xa0</span></p><p><span>Sanders might have tried to provoke an argument, but Clinton was set on extinguishing his attempt to seem like an alternative.\xc2\xa0</span></p></div></div><div class="sharebox sharebox-minute"
